Soul Diseases and Degrees of Prophethood
The author classifies soul powers, states diseases and cures, and defines prophetic rank.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author defines the rational soul's diseases and cures, and how the truthful prophet's rank is determined by his ability to cure these diseases.

Core Idea
The truthful prophet cures souls of turning away from truth and towards creation.

After establishing the two stations of perfection, the author now addresses how the perfected spiritual power benefits others. He first classifies rational souls into four types based on their theoretical and practical powers. Then he identifies the two diseases that afflict souls and their corresponding cures. This leads directly to the definition of the truthful prophet as the one who calls to health, and a hierarchy of prophethood based on effectiveness.

Guided Path
1
Understand the four types of rational souls
Read the passage and note the four possibilities: strong in theory but weak in practice, the opposite, perfect in both, and deficient in both. Recognize that the last type is most common.
This classification sets the stage for the discussion of diseases.
2
Identify the two diseases and two cures
The passage explicitly states the diseases: turning away from truth and turning towards creation. The cures are the opposites: turning towards truth and turning away from creation.
These are the key terms: الإعراض عن الحق and الإقبال على الخلق.
3
Connect the diseases to the definition of the truthful prophet
The truthful prophet is the one who calls creation to the cure (turn towards truth and away from creation). This defines prophethood in terms of healing the soul.
The author is redefining prophethood functionally.
4
Grasp how the degrees of prophethood are determined
The rank of a prophet depends on his ability to impart this health. More effective prophets have higher degrees, weaker ones lower degrees.
This is a hierarchical scale based on success in curing souls.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم بعد الفراغ من هذين المقامين تكون قوته الروحانية ، مؤثرة في تكميل أرواح الناقصين في فوتي النظر والعمل . ولما عرفت أن النفوس الناطقة مختلفة بالماهيات ، فقد تكون بعض النفوس قوية كاملة في القوة النظرية ، وضعيفة في القوة العملية ، وقد تكون بالضد منه ، فتكون قوية في التصرف في أجسام العالم العنصري ، ضعيفة في المعارف النظرية الإلهية. وقد تكون كاملة قاهرة فيهما جميعاً ، وذلك في غاية الندرة ، وقد تكون ناقصة فيهما جميعاً . وذلك هو الغالب في أكثر الخلق . إذا عرفت هذه المقدمات . فنقول : مرض النفوس الناطقة شيئان : الإعراض عن الحق ، والإقبال على الخلق [ وصحتها شيئان : الإقبال على الحق ، والإعراض عن الخلق ] فكل من دعا الخلق إلى الإقبال على الحق [ والإعراض عن الخلق ] فهو النبي الصادق . وقد ذكرنا : أن مراتب هذا النوع من الناس : مختلفة بالقوة والضعف والنقصان، وكل من كانت قدرته على إفادة هذه الصحة ، أكمل ، كان أعلى في درجة النبوة، وكل من كانت درجته في هذا الباب أضعف ، كان انقص في درجة النبوة [ فهذا ما أردنا شرحه وبيانه من حال النبوة . والله أعلم ]
Then after finishing these two stations, his spiritual power becomes effective in perfecting the souls of the deficient in the two powers of contemplation and action. And since you know that the rational souls differ in their essences, some souls may be strong and perfect in the theoretical power but weak in the practical power, and the opposite may occur, so that it is strong in disposing over the bodies of the elemental world but weak in theoretical divine knowledges. And it may be perfect and dominant in both, and that is extremely rare, and it may be deficient in both, and that is prevalent in most of creation. When you have recognized these premisses, we say: The disease of rational souls are two things: turning away from truth and turning towards creation [and their health are two things: turning towards truth and turning away from creation]. So whoever calls creation to turn towards truth [and turn away from creation] is the truthful prophet. And we have mentioned that the ranks of this type of people vary in strength, weakness, and deficiency. And whoever's ability to impart this health is more perfect is higher in the degree of prophethood, and whoever's degree in this matter is weaker is lower in the degree of prophethood. [This is what we intended to explain and clarify concerning the state of prophethood. And God knows best.]
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion on prophethood. The author first notes that after the two stations (theoretical and practical perfection), the perfect man's spiritual power becomes effective in perfecting deficient souls in both theory and practice. He then reminds us that rational souls differ in essence: some are strong in theory but weak in practice, some the opposite, some perfect in both (rare), and some deficient in both (common). After these premisses, he identifies the two diseases of rational souls: turning away from truth and turning towards creation. The two cures are the opposite: turning towards truth and turning away from creation. The truthful prophet is the one who calls creation to truth and away from creation. The ranks of prophets vary in strength and weakness; those more capable of imparting this health are higher in degree, and those weaker are lower. The passage ends with a closing statement that this is the intended explanation of prophethood. The argument builds on the earlier premisses and applies them to define prophethood in terms of curing soul diseases.

Sickness and Health of Rational Souls and Ranks of Prophethood
Defines the two sicknesses and two healths of rational souls and ranks prophets accordingly.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two sicknesses and two healths of rational souls and how they determine the rank of prophethood.

Core Idea
Spiritual health is turning to truth and away from creation; prophets are those who teach this.

This passage from al-Matalib al-Aliyah defines the inner state of rational souls. It begins by noting that theoretical divine knowledges can be perfect or deficient. Then it lists the two forms of sickness and health. Finally, it shows that prophets are those who call others to health, and their rank depends on their ability to impart it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Get a feel for the author's definitions.
2
Identify the two sicknesses and two healths
The passage explicitly states the two sicknesses: turning away from truth and turning towards creation. The two healths are the opposites: turning towards truth and turning away from creation.
3
Connect to prophethood
Notice how the definition of health leads to the definition of a truthful prophet: one who calls creation to turn towards truth and away from creation.
4
Understand ranking of prophets
The passage states that ranks vary based on the ability to impart this health. The more complete the ability, the higher the degree of prophethood.
This is not based on miracles but on transformative power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْمَعَارِفُ النَّظَرِيَّةُ الْإِلَهِيَّةُ. وَقَدْ تَكُونُ كَامِلَةً قَاهِرَةً فِيهِمَا جَمِيعًا، وَذَلِكَ فِي غَايَةِ النُّدْرَةِ، وَقَدْ تَكُونُ نَاقِصَةً فِيهِمَا جَمِيعًا. وَذَلِكَ هُوَ الْغَالِبُ فِي أَكْثَرِ الْخَلْقِ.
إِذَا عَرَفْتَ هَذِهِ الْمُقَدِّمَاتِ. فَنَقُولُ: مَرَضُ النُّفُوسِ النَّاطِقَةِ شَيْئَانِ: الْإِعْرَاضُ عَنِ الْحَقِّ، وَالْإِقْبَالُ عَلَى الْخَلْقِ. وَصِحَّتُهَا شَيْئَانِ: الْإِقْبَالُ عَلَى الْحَقِّ، وَالْإِعْرَاضُ عَنِ الْخَلْقِ. فَكُلُّ مَنْ دَعَا الْخَلْقَ إِلَى الْإِقْبَالِ عَلَى الْحَقِّ وَالْإِعْرَاضِ عَنِ الْخَلْقِ فَهُوَ النَّبِيُّ الصَّادِقُ. وَقَدْ ذَكَرْنَا: أَنَّ مَرَاتِبَ هَذَا النَّوْعِ مِنَ النَّاسِ مُخْتَلِفَةٌ بِالْقُوَّةِ وَالضَّعْفِ وَالنُّقْصَانِ، وَكُلُّ مَنْ كَانَتْ قُدْرَتُهُ عَلَى إِفَادَةِ هَذِهِ الصِّحَّةِ أَكْمَلَ، كَانَ أَعْلَى فِي دَرَجَةِ النُّبُوَّةِ، وَكُلُّ مَنْ كَانَتْ دَرَجَتُهُ فِي هَذَا الْبَابِ أَضْعَفَ، كَانَ أَنْقَصَ فِي دَرَجَةِ النُّبُوَّةِ. فَهَذَا مَا أَرَدْنَا شَرْحَهُ وَبَيَانَهُ مِنْ حَالِ النُّبُوَّةِ. وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.
The theoretical divine knowledges. And they may be complete and dominant in both, and that is extremely rare, and they may be deficient in both. That is the predominant in most of creation. When you have known these premises, we say: The sickness of rational souls is two things: turning away from truth and turning towards creation. And their health is two things: turning towards truth and turning away from creation. So everyone who calls creation to turning towards truth and turning away from creation, he is the truthful prophet. And we have mentioned that the ranks of this type of people vary in strength, weakness, and deficiency, and whoever's ability to impart this health is more complete, he is higher in the degree of prophethood, and whoever's degree in this matter is weaker, he is lower in the degree of prophethood. This is what we intended to explain and clarify concerning the state of prophethood. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage defines the spiritual sickness and health of rational souls (al-nufus al-natiqa) and then applies this to prophethood. It begins by stating that theoretical divine knowledges (al-ma'arif al-nazariyya al-ilahiyya) can be complete and dominant in both knowledge and action, though this is rare, or deficient in both, which is common. Then it defines sickness as two opposites: turning away from truth (al-haqq) and turning towards creation (al-khalq). Health is the opposite: turning towards truth and turning away from creation. The one who calls people to this health is the true prophet (al-nabi al-sadiq). The passage then ranks prophets: the more capable a person is in imparting this health, the higher his degree of prophethood; the weaker his degree, the lower. This concludes the discussion on the nature of prophethood.

Key Terms
النفوس الناطقة
مرض
صحة
الإعراض عن الحق
الإقبال على الخلق
النبي الصادق
درجة النبوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophetic rank is based on miracles alone.
Correction: The passage states that rank is based on the ability to turn souls toward truth and away from creation, not on miracles.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the defining characteristic of a truthful prophet?
A) He performs miracles.
B) He calls creation to turn towards truth and away from creation.
C) He has complete knowledge of divine matters.
D) He is free from all sickness.

Key Takeaway
The health of the rational soul is turning to truth, and prophets are those who guide others to this health; their rank depends on their ability to do so.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, what are the main things that cause you to turn away from truth (al-ḥaqq) and turn towards creation (al-khalq)? Be specific: is it social media, status, relationships, or something else? How can you consciously reverse that direction starting today?
?
This lesson defines a truthful prophet as one who calls people to turn towards truth and away from creation. Who in your life has played that role for you, even if not a prophet? Have you ever tried to be that for someone else? If not, what is holding you back?
?
The rank of prophets varies by their ability to impart spiritual health. Reflect on your own influence: Are you helping those around you turn towards truth or away from it? What concrete step can you take this week to become a better caller to truth?

Prophethood
beginner
5 min
The Qur'anic Order: Divinity Before Prophethood
States the Qur'an's method: prophethood built on divinity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Qur'an establishes prophethood only after first proving divine existence, making the proof of prophethood dependent on the proof of Allah's existence and attributes.

Core Idea
Prophethood proofs in the Qur'an are built on a foundation of divinity proofs.

This lesson focuses on the general Qur'anic method: the Qur'an always begins with establishing divine matters (ilahiyyat) before moving to prophethoods (nubuwwat). This order is not arbitrary but reflects a logical priority: prophethood can only be recognized once the existence and perfection of Allah are affirmed. The passage states this as a consistent custom of the Qur'an.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening claim
Read the first two sentences of the Arabic passage. Notice that the author declares the Qur'anic path to be the most complete method for proving prophethood.
The author is comparing this path to other possible methods.
2
Identify the principle of order
Look for the sentence that states 'الأصل هو الإلهيات، والفرع هو النبوات'. Understand that 'asl' means foundation and 'far'' means branch.
This is a key logical ordering.
3
See how the Qur'an applies this
The author says the Qur'an's custom is to begin with divine matters then proceed to prophethoods. This is a general rule derived from many surahs.
Surah al-A'la is given as an example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ ثَانٍ: أَنَّ الْقُرْآنَ الْعَظِيمَ يَدُلُّ عَلَى أَنَّ هَذَا الطَّرِيقَ هُوَ الطَّرِيقُ الْأَكْمَلُ الْأَفْضَلُ فِي إِثْبَاتِ النُّبُوَّةِ.
اعْلَمْ أَنَّا سَنَذْكُرُ سُوَرًا مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ وَنُفَسِّرُهَا، لِيَظْهَرَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ التَّفْسِيرِ صِحَّةُ هَذَا الطَّرِيقِ الَّذِي ذَكَرْنَاهُ. فَمِنْهَا: سُورَةُ سَبِّحِ اسْمَ رَبِّكَ الْأَعْلَى. فَنَقُولُ: قَدْ عَلِمْتَ أَنَّ الْأَصْلَ هُوَ الْإِلَهِيَّاتُ، وَالْفَرْعَ هُوَ النَّبَوَاتُ. فَلَا جَرَمَ جَرَتِ الْعَادَةُ فِي الْقُرْآنِ أَنَّهُ يَقَعُ الِابْتِدَاءُ بِتَقْرِيرِ الْإِلَهِيَّاتِ، ثُمَّ يَقَعُ الشُّرُوعُ فِي تَقْرِيرِ النَّبَوَاتِ بَعْدَهَا. فَفِي هَذِهِ السُّورَةِ بَدَأَ بِالْإِلَهِيَّاتِ فَقَالَ: (سَبِّحِ اسْمَ رَبِّكَ الْأَعْلَى) وَمَعْنَاهُ: أَنَّهُ أَعْلَى مِنْ مُنَاسَبَةِ جَمِيعِ الْمُمْكِنَاتِ وَمُشَابَهَةِ كُلِّ الْمُحْدَثَاتِ، لِأَنَّهَا مُرَكَّبَةٌ مِنَ الْمَادَّةِ وَالصُّورَةِ بِاعْتِبَارٍ، وَمِنَ الْجِنْسِ وَالْفَصْلِ بِاعْتِبَارٍ ثَانٍ، وَمِنْ قُبُولِ التَّغَيُّرِ وَالْفَنَاءِ، إِمَّا فِي الذَّاتِ، وَإِمَّا فِي الصِّفَاتِ. وَهُوَ سُبْحَانَهُ أَعْلَى مِنْ كُلِّ هَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاءِ فِي كُلِّ هَذِهِ الصِّفَاتِ. وَفِيهِ لَطِيفَةٌ أُخْرَى لَا يُمْكِنُ ذِكْرُهَا.
وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ أَكْثَرَ الدَّلَائِلِ الْمَذْكُورَةِ فِي الْقُرْآنِ عَلَى إِثْبَاتِ الْإِلَهِ تَعَالَى، مَحْصُورَةٌ فِي قَاعِدَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ، وَهِيَ حُدُوثُ الصِّفَاتِ، وَهِيَ إِمَّا فِي الْحَيَوَانَاتِ، وَإِمَّا فِي النَّبَاتِ. وَالْحَيَوَانُ كَذَلِكَ لَهُ بَدَنٌ وَنَفْسٌ. فَقَوْلُهُ: (خَلَقَ فَسَوَّى) إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى مَا فِي أَبْدَانِهَا مِنَ الْعَجَائِبِ. وَقَوْلُهُ: (وَالَّذِي قَدَّرَ فَهَدَى) إِشَارَةٌ
A second chapter: That the Mighty Qur'an indicates that this path is the most complete and most excellent path in proving prophethood. Know that we will mention chapters of the Qur'an and interpret them, so that from that interpretation the correctness of this path which we have mentioned may become apparent. Among them: Surah 'Glorify the name of your Lord, the Most High'. So we say: You have known that the foundation is the divine matters, and the branch is the prophethoods. Therefore, the custom in the Qur'an is that it begins with establishing the divine matters, then proceeds to establishing the prophethoods after them. So in this surah, it began with the divine matters and said: 'Glorify the name of your Lord, the Most High.' And its meaning is that He is above any affinity with all possible things and resemblance to all originated things, because they are composed of matter and form in one respect, and of genus and differentia in a second respect, and of susceptibility to change and annihilation, either in essence or in attributes. And He, glorified, is above all these things in all these attributes. And there is another subtlety in it that cannot be mentioned. And know that most of the proofs mentioned in the Qur'an for establishing God Most High are confined to one principle, which is the temporal origination of attributes (huduth al-sifat), and they are either in animals or in plants. Likewise, the animal has a body and a soul. So His saying: 'He created and proportioned' is an indication of the wonders in their bodies. And His saying: 'And He who determined and guided' is an indication
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage introduces the second chapter of the work, which argues that the Qur'an provides the most complete and excellent path for proving prophethood. The author states that he will interpret several Qur'anic surahs to demonstrate the validity of this path. He begins with Surah al-A'la (Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la). First, he establishes a general rule: in the Qur'an, the foundation (al-asl) is always divine matters (al-ilahiyyat), and the branch (al-far') is prophethoods (al-nubuwwat). The Qur'an typically begins by affirming divinity before discussing prophethood. In this surah, it starts with the command to glorify God's name, explaining that God is above any similarity or affinity with created things, which are composed of matter/form, genus/species, and subject to change and annihilation in essence or attributes. He then notes a subtlety he cannot mention. Next, he states that most Qur'anic proofs for God's existence are based on a single principle: the temporal origination of attributes (huduth al-sifat), which are observed either in animals or in plants. Animals have a body and soul. The verse 'He created and proportioned' points to wonders in animal bodies, and 'He who determined and guided' is an indication (the text cuts off here, so the explanation is incomplete).

Key Terms
الإلهيات
النبويات
الأصل
الفرع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Qur'an proves prophethood independently, without prior proof of God's existence.
Correction: The passage clarifies that prophethood proofs are built on prior divine proofs; the Qur'an always begins with divinity.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between divine matters (ilahiyyat) and prophethoods (nubuwwat) in the Qur'an?
A) They are both equally foundational.
B) Divine matters are the foundation, prophethoods are the branch.
C) Prophethoods are the foundation, divine matters are the branch.
D) There is no fixed relationship.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an's method for proving prophethood always begins by establishing divine existence and attributes as the foundation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you study proofs of prophethood, do you first ensure your heart is firmly anchored in the reality of Allah's existence and attributes? If not, what step will you take today to build that foundation?
?
The Qur'an always begins with divinity before prophethood. Is your own faith built in that order? Or have you tried to cling to prophethood without a solid grounding in tawhid? Examine yourself honestly.
?
If you ever find yourself doubting a prophetic message, could the root be a weak conviction in the One who sent him? What concrete action will you take this week to strengthen your certainty in Allah's attributes?

Interpreting Surah al-A'la: Divine Transcendence and Huduth al-Sifat
Interprets Surah al-A'la to show divine transcendence and introduces huduth al-sifat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Surah al-A'la demonstrates divine transcendence and introduces the principle of temporal origination of attributes (huduth al-sifat) as a key proof for God's existence.

Core Idea
Divine transcendence is shown by contrast with created things, and all Qur'anic proofs are based on huduth al-sifat.

This lesson examines the interpretation of Surah al-A'la (Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la) as presented in the passage. The surah begins with glorifying Allah, which the author interprets as declaring His absolute transcendence above all created things. Created things are composed of matter and form, genus and species, and subject to change and annihilation. Allah is above all that. Then the author reveals that most Qur'anic proofs for God's existence are based on one principle: the temporal origination of attributes (huduth al-sifat), observed in animals and plants.

Guided Path
1
Understand the interpretation of 'Sabbih'
The author explains that 'Glorify the name of your Lord' means declaring Allah above any similarity to created things. List the ways created things are limited.
Created things are composed of matter/form, genus/species, and susceptible to change and annihilation.
2
Note the subtlety not mentioned
The author says there is another subtlety he cannot mention. This teaches that some insights are beyond the scope of this discussion.
Accept the author's discretion.
3
Identify the key principle: huduth al-sifat
The author states that most Qur'anic proofs for God are confined to one principle: the temporal origination of attributes. This is observed in animals and plants.
This principle is crucial in kalam.
4
Link to the verses of Surah al-A'la
The verses 'He created and proportioned' and 'He determined and guided' point to wonders in animal bodies and souls, which are evidences of huduth al-sifat.
The passage ends abruptly; we infer the proofs continue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ ثَانٍ: أَنَّ الْقُرْآنَ الْعَظِيمَ يَدُلُّ عَلَى أَنَّ هَذَا الطَّرِيقَ هُوَ الطَّرِيقُ الْأَكْمَلُ الْأَفْضَلُ فِي إِثْبَاتِ النُّبُوَّةِ.
اعْلَمْ أَنَّا سَنَذْكُرُ سُوَرًا مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ وَنُفَسِّرُهَا، لِيَظْهَرَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ التَّفْسِيرِ صِحَّةُ هَذَا الطَّرِيقِ الَّذِي ذَكَرْنَاهُ. فَمِنْهَا: سُورَةُ سَبِّحِ اسْمَ رَبِّكَ الْأَعْلَى. فَنَقُولُ: قَدْ عَلِمْتَ أَنَّ الْأَصْلَ هُوَ الْإِلَهِيَّاتُ، وَالْفَرْعَ هُوَ النَّبَوَاتُ. فَلَا جَرَمَ جَرَتِ الْعَادَةُ فِي الْقُرْآنِ أَنَّهُ يَقَعُ الِابْتِدَاءُ بِتَقْرِيرِ الْإِلَهِيَّاتِ، ثُمَّ يَقَعُ الشُّرُوعُ فِي تَقْرِيرِ النَّبَوَاتِ بَعْدَهَا. فَفِي هَذِهِ السُّورَةِ بَدَأَ بِالْإِلَهِيَّاتِ فَقَالَ: (سَبِّحِ اسْمَ رَبِّكَ الْأَعْلَى) وَمَعْنَاهُ: أَنَّهُ أَعْلَى مِنْ مُنَاسَبَةِ جَمِيعِ الْمُمْكِنَاتِ وَمُشَابَهَةِ كُلِّ الْمُحْدَثَاتِ، لِأَنَّهَا مُرَكَّبَةٌ مِنَ الْمَادَّةِ وَالصُّورَةِ بِاعْتِبَارٍ، وَمِنَ الْجِنْسِ وَالْفَصْلِ بِاعْتِبَارٍ ثَانٍ، وَمِنْ قُبُولِ التَّغَيُّرِ وَالْفَنَاءِ، إِمَّا فِي الذَّاتِ، وَإِمَّا فِي الصِّفَاتِ. وَهُوَ سُبْحَانَهُ أَعْلَى مِنْ كُلِّ هَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاءِ فِي كُلِّ هَذِهِ الصِّفَاتِ. وَفِيهِ لَطِيفَةٌ أُخْرَى لَا يُمْكِنُ ذِكْرُهَا.
وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ أَكْثَرَ الدَّلَائِلِ الْمَذْكُورَةِ فِي الْقُرْآنِ عَلَى إِثْبَاتِ الْإِلَهِ تَعَالَى، مَحْصُورَةٌ فِي قَاعِدَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ، وَهِيَ حُدُوثُ الصِّفَاتِ، وَهِيَ إِمَّا فِي الْحَيَوَانَاتِ، وَإِمَّا فِي النَّبَاتِ. وَالْحَيَوَانُ كَذَلِكَ لَهُ بَدَنٌ وَنَفْسٌ. فَقَوْلُهُ: (خَلَقَ فَسَوَّى) إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى مَا فِي أَبْدَانِهَا مِنَ الْعَجَائِبِ. وَقَوْلُهُ: (وَالَّذِي قَدَّرَ فَهَدَى) إِشَارَةٌ
A second chapter: That the Mighty Qur'an indicates that this path is the most complete and most excellent path in proving prophethood. Know that we will mention chapters of the Qur'an and interpret them, so that from that interpretation the correctness of this path which we have mentioned may become apparent. Among them: Surah 'Glorify the name of your Lord, the Most High'. So we say: You have known that the foundation is the divine matters, and the branch is the prophethoods. Therefore, the custom in the Qur'an is that it begins with establishing the divine matters, then proceeds to establishing the prophethoods after them. So in this surah, it began with the divine matters and said: 'Glorify the name of your Lord, the Most High.' And its meaning is that He is above any affinity with all possible things and resemblance to all originated things, because they are composed of matter and form in one respect, and of genus and differentia in a second respect, and of susceptibility to change and annihilation, either in essence or in attributes. And He, glorified, is above all these things in all these attributes. And there is another subtlety in it that cannot be mentioned. And know that most of the proofs mentioned in the Qur'an for establishing God Most High are confined to one principle, which is the temporal origination of attributes (huduth al-sifat), and they are either in animals or in plants. Likewise, the animal has a body and a soul. So His saying: 'He created and proportioned' is an indication of the wonders in their bodies. And His saying: 'And He who determined and guided' is an indication
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage introduces the second chapter of the work, which argues that the Qur'an provides the most complete and excellent path for proving prophethood. The author states that he will interpret several Qur'anic surahs to demonstrate the validity of this path. He begins with Surah al-A'la (Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la). First, he establishes a general rule: in the Qur'an, the foundation (al-asl) is always divine matters (al-ilahiyyat), and the branch (al-far') is prophethoods (al-nubuwwat). The Qur'an typically begins by affirming divinity before discussing prophethood. In this surah, it starts with the command to glorify God's name, explaining that God is above any similarity or affinity with created things, which are composed of matter/form, genus/species, and subject to change and annihilation in essence or attributes. He then notes a subtlety he cannot mention. Next, he states that most Qur'anic proofs for God's existence are based on a single principle: the temporal origination of attributes (huduth al-sifat), which are observed either in animals or in plants. Animals have a body and soul. The verse 'He created and proportioned' points to wonders in animal bodies, and 'He who determined and guided' is an indication (the text cuts off here, so the explanation is incomplete).

Key Terms
سورة سبح اسم ربك الأعلى
مادة
صورة
جنس
فصل
حدوث الصفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Qur'anic proofs for God are diverse and unrelated. The author states they are all based on one principle: huduth al-sifat.
Correction: Most Qur'anic proofs are unified under the principle of temporal origination of attributes.

Checkpoint

B) The temporal origination of attributes (huduth al-sifat)
C) The argument from contingency (imkan)
D) The argument from first cause (sababiyyah)

Key Takeaway
Surah al-A'la teaches divine transcendence and points to the principle of huduth al-sifat, which is the core of most Qur'anic proofs for God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'سبح اسم ربك الأعلى' in your prayers, do you genuinely feel that Allah is above every limitation you might imagine, or do you unconsciously picture Him like a powerful human? What would it mean for your worship today to truly internalize that He is above matter, form, change, and annihilation?
?
The passage says that every creature, including you, is composed of matter and form and subject to change and annihilation. How does this reality challenge your attachment to your health, wealth, or status? Are you living as if only Allah is eternal and everything else is perishing?
?
Most proofs for God in the Qur'an come from observing the changes in animals and plants. When you see a bird building a nest or a seed sprouting, do you recognize it as a direct sign of Allah's existence and power, or do you dismiss it as mere nature? What one change will you commit to noticing tomorrow as a proof?

The Four Perfections of Prophets: Knowledge, Action, and Teaching
Razi enumerates and explains the four perfections of prophets with order and priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four perfections that constitute a prophet's complete state, their logical order, and why personal perfection precedes teaching others.

Core Idea
A prophet's completeness has four dimensions: own knowledge, own action, teaching knowledge, teaching action.

After establishing proofs from the natural world, Razi turns to prophethood. He identifies four aspects of prophetic perfection—two internal and two outward—and explains why they must be presented in a specific order. This passage lays out the framework for understanding the prophetic mission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to identify the four perfections. Notice how Razi uses enumeration (أولها, ثانيها, etc.) to structure his argument.
The passage is a classification. Look for the four items.
2
Analyze the order
Razi states that personal perfection in the two powers precedes the ability to perfect others. Also, theoretical power is nobler than practical. Trace how this determines the order of explanation.
Think about why theoretical power is considered nobler.
3
Reflect on the completeness
Consider what it means for a prophet to have reached 'the ultimate end' in prophethood when these four stations are fulfilled. How does this framework apply to the Qur'an's presentation?
This is the final conclusion of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما قرر أمر الإنميات ، أتبعه بتقرير أمر النبوات . وقد علمت أن كمال حال الأنبياء عليهم السلام . في حصول أمور أربعة : أولها : كمال القوة النظرية (١) وثانيها : كمال القوة العملية . وثالثها : قدرته على تكميل القوة النظرية لغيره . [ ورابعها : قدرته على تكميل القوة العملية التي لغيره (۲) ] ولاشك أن كمال حاله في القوتين [ مقدم على قدرته على تكميل غيره في هاتين القوتين (۳) ] ولا شك أن القوة النظرية أشرف من القوة العملية . فهذا البيان يقتضي أن يقع الابتداء أولاً بشرح قوته النظرية . وثانياً بشرح قوته العملية . وثالثا : بكيفية حاله في القدرة على تكميل القوة النظرية التي للناقصين ورابعها : كيفية حالة في القدرة على تكميل القوة العملية التي للناقصين (٤) ] فإذا ظهر كماله في هذه المقامات الأربعة ، فحينئذ يظهر أنه بلغ في صفة النبوة والرسالة إلى الغاية القصوى
When He established the matter of plants, He followed it by establishing the matter of prophethood. And you have known that the complete state of the prophets, peace be upon them, consists in the attainment of four matters: First: perfection of the theoretical power; second: perfection of the practical power; third: his ability to complete the theoretical power of others; [fourth: his ability to complete the practical power of others]. There is no doubt that his own perfection in the two powers precedes his ability to complete others in these two powers. And there is no doubt that the theoretical power is more noble than the practical power. This exposition requires that we begin first by explaining his theoretical power, second by explaining his practical power, third by the manner of his state in the ability to complete the theoretical power of those who are deficient, and fourth by the manner of his state in the ability to complete the practical power of those who are deficient. So when his perfection appears in these four stations, then it appears that he has reached in the attribute of prophethood and messengership the ultimate end.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation. After establishing the proofs for God from plants, the Qur'an moves to prophethood. The complete state of prophets involves four aspects: 1) perfection of their own theoretical power (knowledge), 2) perfection of their own practical power (action), 3) ability to perfect others' theoretical power, 4) ability to perfect others' practical power. The prophet's own perfection in both powers is prior to his ability to perfect others. Also theoretical power is nobler than practical. So the Qur'an's presentation should follow this order: first explain his theoretical power, then practical, then his ability to teach others theoretically, then practically. When these four are complete, he has reached the ultimate degree of prophethood and messengership.

Key Terms
القوة النظرية
القوة العملية
تكميل
النبوات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The four perfections are only about the Prophet's personal virtues, not his mission to teach and guide others.
Correction: Razi includes the ability to perfect others in both theoretical and practical powers as essential to prophetic completeness.

Checkpoint
How many perfections does the author list for the complete state of prophets?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The complete state of prophethood involves personal excellence in knowledge and action, and the ability to impart both to others, with personal perfection taking priority.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

If you genuinely believe that theoretical knowledge is more noble than action, why do you often prioritize doing over learning? What does your daily schedule reveal about your actual hierarchy of values?

Razi says a prophet's own perfection must precede his ability to perfect others. If you desire to be a source of guidance for your family or community, what is the one weakness in your theoretical or practical power that you have been neglecting? Write down a concrete step you will take this week to work on it.

The Prophet's Perfect Theoretical Power: 'We Will Make You Recite, So You Will Not Forget'
Razi interprets the first verse of Surah al-A'la as evidence for theoretical perfection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi interprets the verse 'سنقرئك فلا تنسى' as evidence for the Prophet's perfection in theoretical power, meaning his soul is holy and free from error and forgetfulness.

Core Idea
The Prophet's soul is divinely protected from forgetfulness, showing his perfect theoretical power.

Razi continues his analysis of the four perfections by turning to the Qur'anic evidence. After establishing the principles of divinity, he examines verses from Surah al-A'la that highlight the Prophet's unique gifts. This lesson focuses on the first verse, which addresses the Prophet's recitation and divine guarantee against forgetfulness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how Razi introduces this as the first perfection after mentioning divinity.
The phrase 'إذا عرفت هذا' connects to the previous discussion.
2
Identify the perfection type
The passage explicitly says 'بدأ أولاً بكمال حاله في القوة النظرية'. So this verse is about theoretical perfection.
3
Understand the interpretation
Razi explains that 'سنقرئك فلا تنسى' means the Prophet's soul is holy, safe from error and forgetfulness by divine will, except for what is due to human nature.
The exception 'إلا ما شاء الله' indicates that any forgetfulness is by divine will, not a defect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : إنه تعالى لما ذكر أصول الإلهيات ، وأراد الشروع في صفات النبوة ، بدأ أولاً بكمال حاله في القوة النظرية ، فقال : سنقرئك فلا تنسى ) يعني : أن نفسك نفس قدسية آمنة من الغلط والنسيان إلا ما شاء الله كم أن يحصل بمقتضى الجبلة الإنسانية، والطينة البشرية . ثم أتبعه ببيان كمال حاله في القوة العملية فقال : ( ونيسرك لليسرى ) ومعناه : أنا نقوي دواعيك في الأعمال التي تفيد اليسر والسعادة في الدنيا والآخرة . ثم لما بين كمال حاله في هذين المقامين ، أتبعه بأن أمره بأن يشتغل بتكميل الناقصين، وإرشاد المحتاجين ، فقال : فذكر إن نفعت الذكرى ) فقوله : فذكر ) أمر له بإرشاد الناقصين ، وقوله : ( إن نفعت الذكرى ) [ تنبيه على
If you know this, then we say: When He, exalted, mentioned the principles of divinity and wanted to begin with the attributes of prophethood, He started first with the perfection of his state in the theoretical power, and said: 'We will make you recite, so you will not forget' – meaning that your soul is a holy soul, safe from error and forgetfulness except what Allah wills, as occurs by virtue of human nature and human clay. Then He followed it by explaining the perfection of his state in the practical power, and said: 'And We will ease you to ease' – meaning: We strengthen your motives in deeds that bring ease and happiness in this world and the Hereafter. Then when He made clear his perfection in these two stations, He followed it by commanding him to occupy himself with completing the deficient and guiding the needy, and said: 'So remind, if reminder benefits.' So His statement 'So remind' is a command for him to guide the deficient, and His statement 'if reminder benefits' [is an indication that...
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is an application of the four-perfection scheme to the verses of Surah al-A'la. After establishing divinity, the Qur'an addresses the Prophet's qualities. First, 'We will make you recite, so you will not forget' refers to the perfection of theoretical power – the Prophet's soul is holy, free from error and forgetfulness. Second, 'And We will ease you to ease' refers to the perfection of practical power – strengthening his motives for good deeds. Third, 'So remind, if reminder benefits' commands him to complete the deficient, i.e., to teach and guide others. The phrase 'if reminder benefits' implies that the reminder is beneficial. The text cuts off, but the idea is that these three verses cover the first three perfections: his own knowledge, his own action, and his ability to teach others. The fourth perfection (ability to guide others practically) might be covered elsewhere or in the missing part.

The Prophet's Perfect Practical Power: 'We Will Ease You to Ease'
Razi interprets the second verse of Surah al-A'la as evidence for practical perfection.

The Four Perfections of Prophets
Enumeration of four perfections and their logical order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author identifies the four perfections that constitute prophetic completeness and their logical order.

Core Idea
Prophetic perfection is fourfold: personal knowledge and action, then teaching others both.

Before diving into the Qur'anic proofs, the author first defines the benchmark of prophetic perfection. He asserts that the complete prophetic state rests on four attainments: two personal and two relational. This lesson unpacks that framework and the reason for ordering the perfections as he does.

Guided Path
1
Read the enumeration
Read the passage where the author states the four perfections. Notice he lists them in a specific order and gives a reason for it.
2
Identify the two personal perfections
The first two perfections are personal: theoretical power (knowledge) and practical power (action). The author says theoretical power is nobler than practical power.
3
Identify the two relational perfections
The next two perfections are the ability to perfect others in theoretical and practical powers. Note that personal perfection precedes the ability to perfect others.
4
Understand the logical order
The author argues that explaining the four perfections should follow a specific order: first the prophet's own theoretical power, then his practical power, then his ability to perfect others in these powers. This order reflects both priority and nobility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما قرر أمر الإنميات، أتبعه بتقرير أمر النبوات. وقد علمت أن كمال حال الأنبياء عليهم السلام في حصول أمور أربعة: أولها: كمال القوة النظرية، وثانيها: كمال القوة العملية، وثالثها: قدرته على تكميل القوة النظرية لغيره، [ورابعها: قدرته على تكميل القوة العملية التي لغيره] ولاشك أن كمال حاله في القوتين [مقدم على قدرته على تكميل غيره في هاتين القوتين] ولا شك أن القوة النظرية أشرف من القوة العملية. فهذا البيان يقتضي أن يقع الابتداء أولاً بشرح قوته النظرية، وثانياً بشرح قوته العملية، وثالثاً: بكيفية حاله في القدرة على تكميل القوة النظرية التي للناقصين، ورابعاً: كيفية حاله في القدرة على تكميل القوة العملية التي للناقصين. فإذا ظهر كماله في هذه المقامات الأربعة، فحينئذ يظهر أنه بلغ في صفة النبوة والرسالة إلى الغاية القصوى.
إذا عرفت هذا فنقول: إنه تعالى لما ذكر أصول الإلهيات، وأراد الشروع في صفات النبوة، بدأ أولاً بكمال حاله في القوة النظرية، فقال: (سنقرئك فلا تنسى) يعني: أن نفسك نفس قدسية آمنة من الغلط والنسيان إلا ما شاء الله كم أن يحصل بمقتضى الجبلة الإنسانية، والطينة البشرية. ثم أتبعه ببيان كمال حاله في القوة العملية فقال: (ونيسرك لليسرى) ومعناه: أنا نقوي دواعيك في الأعمال التي تفيد اليسر والسعادة في الدنيا والآخرة. ثم لما بين كمال حاله في هذين المقامين، أتبعه بأن أمره بأن يشتغل بتكميل الناقصين، وإرشاد المحتاجين، فقال: (فذكر إن نفعت الذكرى) فقوله: (فذكر) أمر له بإرشاد الناقصين، وقوله: (إن نفعت الذكرى) تنبيه على أنه ليس كل من سمع ذلك التذكير انتفع به. فإن النفوس الناطقة: مختلفة، فبعضها ينتفع بذلك التذكير، وبعضها لا ينتفع به، وبعضها يضره سماع ذلك التذكير، لأن سماعه يشير في قلبه دواعي الحسد والغيظ والغضب والإصرار على الجهل. ثم لما نبه تعالى على أن المستمع لذلك التذكير قد ينتفع به، وقد لا ينتفع به، أتبعه ببيان خاصية كل واحد من هذين القسمين، فبين أن صفة من ينتفع بهذا التذكير، هو أن يكون الخوف غالباً على قلبه، والخشية مستولية على روحه. ولأجل ذلك الخوف: يطلب زاد المعاد، فلا جرم أنه ينتفع بإرشاد هذا المحق. وأما الذي لا ينتفع بهذا التذكير ويتباعد عنه، ويجتنب من القرب منه، فهو النفس الموصوفة بكونها أشقى النفوس، فإنها تبقى في عناء هذا العالم، وبعد الموت تقع في نيران الحسرة والوحشة. ولما بين هذا أزاله في صفته، فقال: (ثم لا يموت فيها، ولا يحيى) وإنما قال: (ثم لا يموت فيها) لما ثبت أن النفس لا تموت بموت البدن، وإنما قال: (ولا يحيى) لأنها وإن بقيت حية، لكنها بقيت في العذاب. والموت خير من هذه الحياة، فلهذا قال: (ثم لا يموت فيها ولا يحيي) ولما بين من لا ينتفع بذلك التذكير، بين كمال حال من ينتفع به، فقال: (قد أفلح من تزكى) وذلك لأن المقصود من تعليم الأنبياء، وتذكيرهم وإرشادهم: أمران: أحدهما: إزالة الأخلاق الذميمة الجسمانية عن النفس. والثاني: تحصيل الصفات الحميدة الروحانية في النفس، ولما كانت إزالة مالا ينبغي مقدمة على تحصيل ما ينبغي، لا جرم ابتدأ بقوله تعالى: (قد أفلح من تزكى) والمراد منه: تزكية النفس وتطهيرها عن الصفات المذمومة، ولما ذكر ذلك، أتبعه بتحصيل ما ينبغي، وذلك إما في القوة النظرية، أو في القوة العملية. ورئيس المعارف النظرية: ذكر الله تعالى ومعرفته، ورئيس الأعمال الفاضلة: خدمة الله تعالى. فلهذا قال: (وذكر اسم ربه) وهو إشارة إلى استسعاد الإنسان في تكميل قوته
And when he settled the matter of growing things, he followed it by settling the matter of prophecies. And you have known that the perfection of the state of the prophets, peace be upon them, consists in the attainment of four matters: first: perfection of the theoretical power; second: perfection of the practical power; third: his ability to perfect the theoretical power for others; [fourth: his ability to perfect the practical power that belongs to others]. And there is no doubt that the perfection of his state in the two powers [takes precedence over his ability to perfect others in these two powers] and there is no doubt that the theoretical power is nobler than the practical power. This exposition requires that the beginning be made first by explaining his theoretical power, secondly by explaining his practical power, thirdly concerning the modality of his state in the ability to perfect the theoretical power for the deficient, and fourthly concerning the modality of his state in the ability to perfect the practical power for the deficient. And when his perfection appears in these four stations, then it appears that he has reached in the attribute of prophethood and messengership the ultimate extreme. If you understand this, then we say: verily, He, exalted, when He mentioned the principles of the divine matters and intended to begin on the attributes of prophethood, He started first with the perfection of his state in theoretical power, and said: 'We shall teach you and you shall not forget' – meaning that your soul is a holy soul safe from error and forgetfulness, except what God wills, as occurs by necessity of human disposition and human nature. Then He followed it by explaining the perfection of his state in the practical power and said: 'And We shall ease you towards ease' – and its meaning is: We strengthen your motivations in deeds that bring ease and happiness in this world and the Hereafter. Then when He explained the perfection of his state in these two stations, He followed it by commanding him to occupy himself with perfecting the deficient and guiding the needy, and said: 'So remind, if the reminder benefits' – so His saying 'so remind' is a command to him to guide the deficient, and His saying 'if the reminder benefits' is a notification that not everyone who hears that reminder benefits from it. For the rational souls are different: some of them benefit from that reminder, some do not benefit from it, and some are harmed by hearing that reminder, because hearing it stirs in their hearts the motives of envy, rage, anger, and persistence in ignorance. Then when He, exalted, notified that the hearer of that reminder may benefit from it and may not benefit from it, He followed it by explaining the property of each of these two categories, and He clarified that the attribute of one who benefits from this reminder is that fear predominates in his heart and awe overcomes his spirit. And because of that fear, he seeks provision for the return, so inevitably he benefits from the guidance of this truth-teller. But as for one who does not benefit from this reminder and keeps away from it and avoids nearness to it, he is the soul described as being the most wretched of souls; it remains in the toil of this world and after death falls into the fires of regret and desolation. And when He explained this, He removed him from his attribute and said: 'Then he will not die therein, nor will he live.' And He only said 'then he will not die therein' because it is established that the soul does not die with the death of the body, and He only said 'nor will he live' because although it remains alive, it remains in punishment. And death is better than this life; therefore He said: 'Then he will not die therein nor live.' And when He explained who does not benefit from that reminder, He explained the perfect state of one who benefits from it and said: 'He has succeeded who purifies himself.' And that is because the purpose of the teaching of the prophets, their reminding, and their guidance are two matters: first: removal of blameworthy bodily characteristics from the soul; second: acquisition of praiseworthy spiritual characteristics in the soul. And since removal of what should not be is a prerequisite to the acquisition of what should be, inevitably He began with His saying, exalted: 'He has succeeded who purifies himself' and what is meant by it is purification of the soul and its cleansing from blameworthy characteristics. And when He mentioned that, He followed it by the acquisition of what should be, and that is either in the theoretical power or in the practical power. And the chief of theoretical sciences is the remembrance of God, exalted, and knowledge of Him, and the chief of virtuous deeds is the service of God, exalted. Therefore He said: 'And he mentions the name of his Lord,' and that is an indication of man's felicity in perfecting his power...
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the four perfections that constitute the complete state of prophets, followed by a detailed verse-by-verse proof from the Qur'an. The author first asserts that prophetic perfection consists of four things: (1) perfection of theoretical power (knowledge free from error), (2) perfection of practical power (actions leading to ease and happiness), (3) ability to perfect others' theoretical power, and (4) ability to perfect others' practical power. He notes that the prophet's own perfection in the first two powers is a necessary condition for his ability to perfect others, and that theoretical power is superior to practical power. Consequently, the explanation must follow this order. Then he turns to the Qur'anic evidence: the verse 'We shall teach you and you shall not forget' proves the perfection of theoretical power – the prophet's soul is divinely protected from error and forgetfulness. The verse 'And We shall ease you towards ease' proves perfection of practical power – God strengthens his motivations for actions that lead to ease and happiness. The verse 'So remind, if the reminder benefits' commands him to engage in perfecting others; the conditional phrase indicates that benefit is not universal. The author then explains that rational souls differ: some benefit from the reminder, some do not, and some are harmed by it because it incites envy, anger, and ignorance. God then clarifies the characteristics of each group: those who benefit have predominant fear and awe, so they seek provision for the afterlife and accept guidance. Those who do not benefit are described as the most wretched souls; they suffer in this world and after death fall into the fires of regret and desolation, suffering a life that is worse than death, as indicated by the verse 'Then he will not die therein, nor will he live.' Finally, the author explains that the purpose of prophetic teaching is twofold: removal of blameworthy bodily traits (purification) and acquisition of praiseworthy spiritual traits. This is the meaning of 'He has succeeded who purifies himself.' After purification, one acquires theoretical knowledge (remembrance and knowledge of God) and practical virtue (service of God), as indicated by the verse 'And he mentions the name of his Lord.' The passage is cut off at the end.

Key Terms
النبوة (prophethood)
القوة النظرية (theoretical power)
القوة العملية (practical power)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many perfections constitute the complete state of prophets?
A) Two: theoretical and practical
B) Three: knowledge, action, and teaching
C) Four: theoretical power, practical power, ability to perfect others in both
D) Five: the above plus miracles and intercession

Key Takeaway
Prophetic perfection consists of personal knowledge and action, plus the capacity to impart these to others, with theoretical knowledge holding greater nobility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you genuinely prioritize acquiring correct knowledge before acting, or do you often act without understanding? What steps will you take today to ensure your knowledge comes before your practice?
?
Have you ever attempted to teach or advise others while neglecting your own personal growth in knowledge and righteousness? Will you commit to focusing on your own perfection first?
?
Which of the four perfections do you lack most: personal theoretical, personal practical, teaching others theoretically, or teaching others practically? What concrete action will you take this week to address that deficiency?

Prophethood
intermediate
8 min
Quranic Evidence for the Four Perfections
Interpretation of Quranic verses proving the four perfections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author interprets four Quranic verses from Surah Al-A'la as proof of the four perfections of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
Each of the four perfections is proven by a specific Quranic verse.

Having established the framework of four perfections, the author now turns to the Qur'an to demonstrate that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) indeed possessed them. He selects verses from Surah Al-A'la, explaining how each corresponds to one of the perfections. He also discusses how different souls respond to prophetic teaching.

Guided Path
1
Read the first two verses and their explanations
The author uses 'We shall teach you and you shall not forget' to prove the perfection of theoretical power, and 'We shall ease you towards ease' to prove practical power. Note how he explains each.
2
Read the third verse and its elaboration
The verse 'So remind, if the reminder benefits' proves the prophet's role in perfecting others. The author then explains that not all listeners benefit: rational souls are of different types.
3
Understand the three types of souls
The passage categorizes listeners: those who benefit, those who do not benefit, and those who are harmed. The author describes each and cites verses about the wretched soul and the successful soul.
4
Conclude with the two purposes of prophetic teaching
The final part discusses purification (tazkiya) and remembrance of God, which correspond to removal of bad traits and acquisition of good traits in theoretical and practical powers.

Commentary

Checkpoint
Which verse does the author use to prove the perfection of the prophet's practical power?
A) 'We shall teach you and you shall not forget'
B) 'We shall ease you towards ease'
C) 'So remind, if the reminder benefits'
D) 'He has succeeded who purifies himself'

Key Takeaway
Surah Al-A'la provides a complete proof for all four prophetic perfections: the prophet's own knowledge and action, and his mission to teach and guide others, with different responses from different souls.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the Quran being recited or a reminder given, do you notice fear and awe overtaking your heart, or do you find yourself indifferent like those described as 'the most wretched of souls'? What specific change can you make today to ensure you are among those who seek provision for the return?
?
The passage teaches that the purpose of prophetic teaching is to remove blameworthy traits from your soul and acquire praiseworthy ones. Which blameworthy trait—envy, anger, or persistence in ignorance—do you see most clearly in yourself? What concrete step will you take this week to begin removing it?
?
You have just learned that the happiness of man lies in perfecting his power through remembrance and service of God. Are you truly spending your time on what you know is most important—remembering God and serving Him—or are you filling your days with distractions that will leave you empty? What will you do tomorrow to prioritize your soul's perfection?

The Antidote of Four in Surah al-Asr
Author explains the four elements of Surah al-Asr as a spiritual antidote proving prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author interprets Surah al-Asr to reveal a spiritual antidote comprising four elements that constitute the proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
The four elements of Surah al-Asr form a spiritual antidote that proves prophethood.

In this lesson, we explore the author's unique approach to proving prophethood by analyzing Surah al-Asr. He argues that human beings are in loss due to the overwhelming worldly powers in their bodies, but those who take the 'antidote of the four'—faith, righteous deeds, enjoining truth, and enjoining patience—are saved. This antidote corresponds to the perfection of theoretical and practical faculties, both for oneself and others.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Surah al-Asr
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how the author starts by explaining why mankind is in loss.
2
Identify the nineteen powers
The author lists nineteen powers that drag a person to worldly pleasures. Find them in the text and note their grouping.
He mentions external senses, internal senses, appetite, anger, and seven vegetative powers.
3
Understand the intellect's role
The intellect is described as a weak lamp that arises after these powers dominate. Reflect on why this supports the idea of loss.
4
Examine the four components of the antidote
The author extracts from the verse 'except those who believe and do righteous deeds...' four components corresponding to perfecting theoretical and practical faculties for oneself and others. Note how 'patience' is specified.
Patience counteracts appetite and anger which are greatest trials.
5
Connect to prophethood proof
Consider how this analysis serves as a proof of prophethood. The Prophet’s message provides this antidote, thus rescuing humanity from loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن جملة السور اللائقة بهذا المعنى سورة العصر . فبدأ بقوله : ( إن الإنسان لفي خسر ) وذلك لأنا بينا أنه حصل في بدنه تسعة عشر نوعاً من أنواع القوى ، وكلها تجره إلى الدنيا وطيباتها ولذاتها. وهي الحواس الخمس الظاهرة ، والخمس الباطنة ، والشهوة والغضب ، والسبعة النباتية . فمجموعها تسعة عشر ، وهي الزبانية الواقفة على باب جهنم : الجسد
·
وأما العقل ، فإنه مصباح ضعيف . إنما حصل بعد استيلاء تلك التسعة عشر على مملكة البدن ، وإذا كان كذلك ، فالظاهر أن حب الدنيا يستولي على النفوس والأرواح . فإذا مات البدن ، بقيت النفس في الخسران والحرمان فلهذا قال : ( إن الإنسان لفي خسر ) ثم إنه استثنى من هذا الخسران ، إنساناً يتناول ترياق الأربعة ، وهو ترياق روحاني من أخلاط أربعة روحانية . أولها : كمال القوة النظرية ، وهو قوله : ( إلا الذين آمنوا ) وثانيها : كمال القوة العملية وهو قوله : ( وعلموا الصالحات ) وثالثها : السعي في تكميل القوة النظرية للغير، وهو قوله : ( وتواصوا بالحق ) ورابعها : السعي في تكميل القوة العملية للغير ، وهو قوله : ( وتواصوا بالصبر ) وإنما عين الصبر ، لأن البلاء الأكبر في دعاء الشهوة إلى الفساد ، والغضب إلى الإيذاء ، وسفك الدماء ، كما أخبر عن الملائكة أنهم قالوا : أتجعل فيها من يفسد فيها ويسفك ( الدماء ) ؟(٢) فإذا قدر الإنسان على الصبر ، عن إجابة الشهرة والغضب ، فقد فاز بكل الخيرات في القوة العملية :
ومن جملة الآيات الدالة على صحة ما ذكرناه : أنه تعالى حكى عن الكفار أنهم طلبوا منه المعجزات القاهرة في قوله : ( وقالوا : لن نؤمن لك حتى تفجر لنا من الأرض ينبوعاً(٣) ) ثم إنه تعالى قاله له : ( قل : سبحان ربي . هل كنت إلا بشراً رسولاً ) ؟ يعني : كون الشخص إنساناً موصوفاً بالرسالة ، معناه : كونه كاملاً في قوته النظرية والعملية ، وقادراً على معالجة الناقصين في هاتين القوتين . وليس من شرط حصول هذه الصفة ، كونه قادراً على الأحوال التي طلبتموها مني
·
ومن جملة الآيات الدالة على صحة ما ذكرناه أيضاً : أنه تعالى لما قال في سورة الشعراء : ( وإنه لتنزيل رب العالمين ) (١) أورد عليه سؤالاً ، وهو أنه : لم لا يجوز أن يكون هذا من تنزيل الشياطين ؟ فقال جواباً عنه : ( وما تنزلت به الشياطين ) ثم بين الجواب ، فقال : هل أنبئكم على من تنزل الشياطين ؟ تنزل على كل أفاك أثيم ) والمعنى: أنه إن كانت الدعوة إلى طلب الدنيا (٢) وطلب اللذات والشهوات، كان ذلك الداعي أفاكاً أثيماً ، والذين يعينونه عليه هم الشياطين . وأما أنا فأدعو إلى الله ، وإلى الإعراض عن الدنيا ، والإقبال على الآخرة ، ولا يكون هذا [ بإعانة الشياطين(۳) ] بل بإعانة الله تعالي . فاستدل بكون دعوته إلى الله تعالى وإلى الحق ، على كونه نبياً صادقاً ، لا ساحراً خبيثاً . ولما أورد عليه سؤالاً آخر ، وهو : أن لكل واحد من الشعراء شيطاناً يعينه على شعره ، فلم لا يجوز أن يكون حالك كذلك ؟ أجاب عنه بقوله : ( والشعراء يتبعهم الغاوون [ألم تر أنهم في كل واد يهيمون ) والمعنى : أن الشاعر إنما يدعو إلى الطمع في الدنيا وإلى الترغيب في اللذات البدنية ، وأما أنا فأدعو إلى الله تعالى وإلى الدار الآخرة ، فامتنع أن يكون الناصر والمعين في هذه الطريقة : هو الشياطين .
فظهر الفرق وقد ظهر بهذه الآيات : أن الطريق الذي ذكرناه في إثبات النبوة هو الطريق الأكمل الأفضل [ والله أعلم (٤) ] .
And among the sūrahs suitable for this meaning is Sūrat al-‘Aṣr. He began with His statement: 'Indeed, mankind is in loss' because we have shown that there occur in his body nineteen types of powers, all of which drag him to the world and its pleasures and delights. They are the five external senses, the five internal senses, appetite and anger, and the seven vegetative ones. Their total is nineteen, and they are the zabāniyah (angels of punishment) standing at the door of Hell: the body. As for the intellect, it is a weak lamp. It only arises after those nineteen have taken over the kingdom of the body. If that is the case, then it is apparent that love of the world overpowers souls and spirits. So when the body dies, the soul remains in loss and deprivation. Therefore He said: 'Indeed, mankind is in loss.' Then He excepted from this loss a person who takes the antidote of the four, which is a spiritual antidote composed of four spiritual ingredients. The first of them: perfection of the theoretical faculty, which is His statement: 'except those who believe'; the second: perfection of the practical faculty, which is His statement: 'and do righteous deeds'; the third: striving to perfect the theoretical faculty for others, which is His statement: 'and enjoin truth upon one another'; the fourth: striving to perfect the practical faculty for others, which is His statement: 'and enjoin patience upon one another.' He specified patience because the greatest trial is in the call of appetite to corruption and anger to harm and bloodshed, as He informed about the angels when they said: 'Will You place therein one who causes corruption therein and sheds blood?' So if a person is able to exercise patience by not responding to appetite and anger, he has achieved all good in the practical faculty. And among the verses that indicate the correctness of what we have mentioned: that He, exalted, related about the disbelievers that they demanded from him overwhelming miracles in His statement: 'And they say: We will not believe you until you break open for us from the earth a spring.' Then He, exalted, said to him: 'Say: Exalted is my Lord! Was I ever but a human messenger?' Meaning: the fact that a person is a human described with messengerhood means that he is perfect in his theoretical and practical faculties, and capable of treating those deficient in these two faculties. It is not a condition for obtaining this attribute that he be able to do the things you requested from me. And among the verses indicating the correctness of what we have mentioned also: that when He, exalted, said in Sūrat al-Shu‘arā': 'And indeed it is the revelation of the Lord of the worlds,' an objection was raised against it, namely: Why is it not possible that this is from the revelation of the devils? So He replied to it: 'And the devils have not brought it down.' Then He clarified the answer, saying: 'Shall I inform you upon whom the devils descend? They descend upon every sinful liar.' The meaning: If the call was for seeking the world and seeking pleasures and appetites, then that caller would be a sinful liar, and those who assist him in it are the devils. But I call to God, to turning away from the world, and to focusing on the Hereafter, and this is not with the help of the devils, but with the help of God, exalted. So he used the fact that his call is to God and to the truth as evidence that he is a truthful prophet, not a wicked sorcerer. And when another objection was raised against him, namely: For every poet there is a devil that assists him in his poetry, so why is it not possible that your situation be similar? He replied with His statement: 'And the poets – the erring follow them. Do you not see that they wander in every valley?' The meaning: The poet only calls to greed for the world and to encouragement of bodily pleasures, while I call to God, exalted, and to the abode of the Hereafter. Thus it is impossible that the helper and assistant in this way be the devils. So the difference became clear, and it has become evident through these verses that the way we have mentioned in establishing prophethood is the most complete and best way. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is an argument for the proof of prophethood using Quranic verses. The author begins by explaining that Sūrat al-‘Aṣr is particularly suited for this purpose. He notes that God's statement 'Indeed, mankind is in loss' refers to the nineteen types of powers in the human body (external senses, internal senses, appetite, anger, and seven vegetative faculties) that drag a person toward worldly pleasures, leaving the soul in loss after death. The intellect is described as a weak lamp overwhelmed by these powers. However, God excepts those who take the 'antidote of the four'—a spiritual cure composed of four elements corresponding to the perfections of theoretical and practical faculties, both for oneself and for others. These are faith (perfection of theoretical faculty), righteous deeds (perfection of practical faculty), enjoining truth (perfecting theoretical faculty for others), and enjoining patience (perfecting practical faculty for others). Patience is singled out because it counteracts the greatest trials of appetite and anger. The author then supports his method by citing other verses: from Sūrat al-Isrā', where disbelievers demanded miracles, and God responded that the messenger is merely a human with perfect theoretical and practical faculties, not necessarily a performer of miracles; and from Sūrat al-Shu‘arā', where objections about revelation from devils are refuted by pointing out that the call of the Prophet is to God and the Hereafter, whereas devils assist those who call to worldly pleasures. Thus the author concludes that his method—establishing prophethood through the perfection of faculties and the nature of the call—is the most complete and best way.

القوة العملية

According to the author, what are the four components of the spiritual antidote mentioned in Surah al-Asr?
A) Faith, righteous deeds, enjoining truth, enjoining patience
B) Belief in God, prayer, fasting, charity

D) The five senses, intellect, appetite, anger

Key Takeaway
The four elements of Surah al-Asr—faith, righteous deeds, enjoining truth, and enjoining patience—form a spiritual antidote that demonstrates the perfection of the Prophet's message and thus proves his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage lists nineteen powers that drag you to the world. Which one of these—your external senses, appetite, or anger—has most recently overpowered you, and what did you lose in that moment?
?
You believe the intellect is strong, but the source calls it a 'weak lamp.' In what area of your life have you trusted your reasoning over the clear guidance of the Quran and Sunnah, and what was the result?
?
The antidote includes enjoining patience on others. Think of one person you interact with regularly who struggles with controlling their temper or desires. What specific step will you take this week to remind them of patience, even if it is uncomfortable?

Supporting Proofs from Surah al-Isra' and al-Shu'ara'
Author supports his method with verses from Surah al-Isra' and al-Shu'ara'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses other Quranic verses to support his method of proving prophethood through the nature of the Prophet's call and his perfect faculties.

Core Idea
The Prophet's call to God and the Hereafter, not miracles, is the decisive proof of prophethood.

In this lesson, we continue with the author's argument by examining two additional Quranic passages. From Surah al-Isra', he argues that the Prophet is a human with perfect theoretical and practical faculties, not necessarily a miracle worker. From Surah al-Shu'ara', he refutes the objection that revelation could come from devils by contrasting the Prophet's call to God and the Hereafter with the poets' call to worldly pleasures.

Guided Path
1
Read the passages from Surah al-Isra' and al-Shu'ara'
Read the Arabic and translation of the second part of the source, which includes these verses.
2
Understand the argument from Surah al-Isra'
The disbelievers demanded miracles, but God's response shows that being a prophet does not require performing such miracles; it requires being perfect in theoretical and practical faculties and teaching others.
3
Analyze the refutation in Surah al-Shu'ara'
The objection that revelation could be from devils is refuted by pointing out that devils assist those who call to worldly pleasures, whereas the Prophet calls to God and the Hereafter.
The response uses the content of the call as evidence.
4
Connect the two arguments
Both arguments support the author's method: the proof of prophethood lies in the perfection of the prophet's faculties and the nature of his call, not in miracles.
5
Appreciate the conclusion
The author concludes that his way is the most complete and best way to establish prophethood.

The intellect is described as a weak lamp overwhelmed by these powers. However, God excepts those who take the 'antidote of the four'—a spiritual cure composed of four elements corresponding to the perfections of theoretical and practical faculties, both for oneself and for others. These are faith (perfection of theoretical faculty), righteous deeds (perfection of practical faculty), enjoining truth (perfecting theoretical faculty for others), and enjoining patience (perfecting practical faculty for others). Patience is singled out because it counteracts the greatest trials of appetite and anger. The author then supports his method by citing other verses: from Sūrat al-Isrā', where disbelievers demanded miracles, and God responded that the messenger is merely a human with perfect theoretical and practical faculties, not necessarily a performer of miracles; and from Sūrat al-Shu‘arā', where objections about revelation from devils are refuted by pointing out that the call of the Prophet is to God and the Hereafter, whereas devils assist those who call to worldly pleasures. Thus the author concludes that his method—establishing prophethood through the perfection of faculties and the nature of the call—is the most complete and best way.

Key Terms
المعجزة
النبوة
الشعراء
الشياطين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the proof of prophethood depends solely on miracles.
Correction: The author shows that the nature of the message and the character of the prophet, as evidenced by his call to God and the Hereafter and his perfect faculties, are more fundamental proofs.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the objection that revelation could come from devils?
A) By citing a miracle performed by the Prophet
B) By arguing that devils assist those who call to worldly pleasures, while the Prophet calls to God and the Hereafter
C) By saying that the Quran is inimitable
D) By pointing out that the Prophet was illiterate

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's call to God and the Hereafter, combined with his perfect faculties, serves as a more fundamental proof of prophethood than miracles alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of someone whose sincerity deeply affects you. Is it because of their miracles or because of the purity of their message and life? How does the Prophet’s example shift what you look for as proof of truth?
?
You often recite or hear the Qur'an. When its verses strike your heart, do you attribute that to God or do you ever doubt its source? How does the argument from the content of the call reinforce your certainty today?
?
If you were asked to prove that Muhammad (peace be upon him) is a true prophet without mentioning any miracle, could you do it using the lesson you just studied? Take a moment to formulate your answer in your own words, ready to share.

Proof of Prophethood from Surah Ash-Shu'ara
Author derives proof of prophethood from Quranic verses on sorcery and poetry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses the Qur'anic discourse in Surah Ash-Shu'ara to prove the Prophet's truthfulness by distinguishing his call from that of sorcerers and poets.

Core Idea
The Prophet's message itself—calling to Allah and the Hereafter—is proof he is not assisted by devils.

The author presents a powerful argument from the Qur'an itself: the Prophet's call is fundamentally different from the calls of sorcerers and poets, who are aided by devils. By analyzing the verses of Surah Ash-Shu'ara, he shows that the content of the Prophet's message—denying worldly pleasures and inviting to the afterlife—cannot originate from evil sources. This lesson walks through the dialectical structure of this proof.

Guided Path
1
Understand the first objection
Read how the objection is raised: the revelation could be from devils. Then see the Qur'anic response: devils only descend on sinful liars.
The response distinguishes the Prophet from those who seek worldly gain.
2
Understand the second objection
Read the comparison to poets, who have devils assisting them. Then see the Qur'anic response: poets call to worldly desires, while the Prophet calls to Allah and the Hereafter.
This further establishes the purity of the Prophet's message.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Notice how the author concludes that this method of proving prophethood is the most complete and best.
This highlights the strength of arguments based on the content of the message.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن جملة الآيات الدالة على صحة ما ذكرناه أيضاً : أنه تعالى لما قال في سورة الشعراء : ( وإنه لتنزيل رب العالمين ) أورد عليه سؤالاً ، وهو أنه : لم لا يجوز أن يكون هذا من تنزيل الشياطين ؟ فقال جواباً عنه : ( وما تنزلت به الشياطين ) ثم بين الجواب ، فقال : هل أنبئكم على من تنزل الشياطين ؟ تنزل على كل أفاك أثيم ) والمعنى: أنه إن كانت الدعوة إلى طلب الدنيا وطلب اللذات والشهوات، كان ذلك الداعي أفاكاً أثيماً ، والذين يعينونه عليه هم الشياطين . وأما أنا فأدعو إلى الله ، وإلى الإعراض عن الدنيا ، والإقبال على الآخرة ، ولا يكون هذا [ بإعانة الشياطين ] بل بإعانة الله تعالي . فاستدل بكون دعوته إلى الله تعالى وإلى الحق ، على كونه نبياً صادقاً ، لا ساحراً خبيثاً . ولما أورد عليه سؤالاً آخر ، وهو : أن لكل واحد من الشعراء شيطاناً يعينه على شعره ، فلم لا يجوز أن يكون حالك كذلك ؟ أجاب عنه بقوله : ( والشعراء يتبعهم الغاوون [ألم تر أنهم في كل واد يهيمون ) والمعنى : أن الشاعر إنما يدعو إلى الطمع في الدنيا وإلى الترغيب في اللذات البدنية ، وأما أنا فأدعو إلى الله تعالى وإلى الدار الآخرة ، فامتنع أن يكون الناصر والمعين في هذه الطريقة : هو الشياطين . فظهر الفرق وقد ظهر بهذه الآيات : أن الطريق الذي ذكرناه في إثبات النبوة هو الطريق الأكمل الأفضل [ والله أعلم ] .
And among the verses indicating the correctness of what we have mentioned also: that He, exalted, when He said in Surat Ash-Shu'ara: 'And indeed it is a revelation of the Lord of the worlds,' a question was raised against Him: why is it not possible that this is from the revelation of the devils? So He answered: 'And the devils have not brought it down.' Then He explained the answer, saying: 'Shall I inform you upon whom the devils descend? They descend upon every sinful liar.' And the meaning: if the call is to seeking the world and seeking pleasures and desires, then that caller is a sinful liar, and those who assist him are the devils. But as for me, I call to Allah, and to turning away from the world, and turning towards the Hereafter, and this is not with the assistance of the devils, but with the assistance of Allah, exalted. So He inferred from His call to Allah and to the truth that He is a truthful prophet, not an evil sorcerer. And when another question was raised against Him: that each poet has a devil that assists him in his poetry, so why is it not possible that your case is likewise? He answered with His saying: 'And the poets – the erring follow them. Do you not see that they wander in every valley?' And the meaning: that the poet only calls to greed in the world and to encouragement in bodily pleasures, but as for me, I call to Allah, exalted, and to the abode of the Hereafter, so it is impossible that the helper and assistant in this way is the devils. So the difference became clear, and it has become clear by these verses that the way we mentioned in proving prophethood is the most complete and best way, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood presented by the author using verses from Surah Ash-Shu'ara. The author enters into a dialectical exchange: God reveals the Qur'an, and a skeptical questioner objects that it might be from devils. God refutes this by stating that devils only descend on sinful liars, not on one who calls to Allah and the Hereafter. The Prophet's very message—turning from worldly desires to the afterlife—is evidence that he is not assisted by devils but by Allah. A second objection compares the Prophet to poets who are aided by devils. The Prophet's response distinguishes his call (to Allah and the Hereafter) from poets' calls (to worldly greed and pleasures). Thus, the Prophet's content is pure, and his helper cannot be devils. The author concludes that this method of proving prophethood is the most excellent.

Key Terms
نبوة
آيات
سورة الشعراء
دعوة
صدق
شياطين
شعراء
شيطان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only miracles can prove a prophet's truthfulness.
Correction: The Qur'an itself argues that the content of the message—calling to Allah and the Hereafter—is incompatible with being assisted by devils, thus proving prophethood.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes the Prophet from a poet?
A) The Prophet uses rhymed prose, while poets use meter.
B) The Prophet calls to Allah and the Hereafter, while poets call to worldly gains.

D) The Prophet performed miracles, while poets do not.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's call to Allah and the Hereafter stands as self-evident proof that he is not a sorcerer or poet aided by devils.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The passage shows that the content of the message proves its source. What does the content of your daily conversations—what you desire and promote—reveal about the source of your inspiration?
?
If the devils only descend on sinful liars who call to worldly pleasures, then examine your own heart: are you, in any aspect of your life, calling yourself or others to the world? What would it take to align your call entirely with the Prophet's call?
